# Excalidraw Data

## Text Elements
Technically these are all equally likely since the order doesnt affect the final probability. the same ammount of each type of ball is chosen each time
Therefore we could have just found the probability of one and then multiplied it by the 4 total possible ways to get that outcome to find
the final probability.  ^HIngDgZV

Suppose we know that 70% of teenagers attend school  ^mGyC4f50

and n=4 ^PuKsh6De

if 0.7 is our mean, then one standard deviation before this is 0.7-0.1025, and one after it is 0.7+0.1025 ^9L93bUNd

There are 20 in our sample, so we are going to multiply the chance that they are in these bounds by the population size. ^DE6EhJtv
